    15	struct ParameterInfo;
    16	
    17	// Information on ranges of registers already claimed/used
    18	struct UsedRange
    19	{
    20	    // What parameter has claimed this range?
    21	    VarLayout* parameter;
    22	
    23	    // Begin/end of the range (half-open interval)
    24	    UInt begin;
    25	    UInt end;
    26	};
    27	bool operator<(UsedRange left, UsedRange right)
    28	{
    29	    if (left.begin != right.begin)
    30	        return left.begin < right.begin;
    31	    if (left.end != right.end)
    32	        return left.end < right.end;
    33	    return false;
    34	}
    35	
    36	static bool rangesOverlap(UsedRange const& x, UsedRange const& y)
    37	{
    38	    SLANG_ASSERT(x.begin <= x.end);
    39	    SLANG_ASSERT(y.begin <= y.end);
    40	
    41	    // If they don't overlap, then one must be earlier than the other,
    42	    // and that one must therefore *end* before the other *begins*
    43	
    44	    if (x.end <= y.begin)
    45	        return false;
    46	    if (y.end <= x.begin)
    47	        return false;
    48	
    49	    // Otherwise they must overlap
    50	    return true;
    51	}
    52	
    53	
    54	struct UsedRanges
    55	{
    56	    // The `ranges` array maintains a sorted list of `UsedRange`
    57	    // objects such that the `end` of a range is <= the `begin`
    58	    // of any range that comes after it.
    59	    //
    60	    // The values covered by each `[begin,end)` range are marked
    61	    // as used, and anything not in such an interval is implicitly
    62	    // free.
    63	    //
    64	    // TODO: if it ever starts to matter for performance, we
    65	    // could encode this information as a tree instead of an array.
    66	    //
    67	    List<UsedRange> ranges;
    68	
    69	    // Add a range to the set, either by extending
    70	    // existing range(s), or by adding a new one.
    71	    //
    72	    // If we find that the new range overlaps with
    73	    // an existing range for a *different* parameter
    74	    // then we return that parameter so that the
    75	    // caller can issue an error.
    76	    //
    77	    VarLayout* Add(UsedRange range)
    78	    {
    79	        // The invariant on entry to this
    80	        // function is that the `ranges` array
    81	        // is sorted and no two entries in the
    82	        // array intersect. We must preserve
    83	        // that property as a postcondition.
    84	        //
    85	        // The other postcondition is that the
    86	        // interval covered by the input `range`
    87	        // must be marked as consumed.
    88	
    89	        // We will try track any parameter associated
    90	        // with an overlapping range that doesn't
    91	        // match the parameter on `range`, so that
    92	        // the compiler can issue useful diagnostics.
    93	        //
    94	        VarLayout* newParam = range.parameter;
    95	        VarLayout* existingParam = nullptr;
    96	
    97	        // A clever algorithm might use a binary
    98	        // search to identify the first entry in `ranges`
    99	        // that might overlap `range`, but we are going
   100	        // to settle for being less clever for now, in
   101	        // the hopes that we can at least be correct.
   102	        //
   103	        // Note: we are going to iterate over `ranges`
   104	        // using indices, because we may actually modify
   105	        // the array as we go.
   106	        //
   107	        Int rangeCount = ranges.getCount();
   108	        for (Int rr = 0; rr < rangeCount; ++rr)
   109	        {
   110	            auto existingRange = ranges[rr];
   111	
   112	            // The invariant on entry to each loop
   113	            // iteration will be that `range` does
   114	            // *not* intersect any preceding entry
   115	            // in the array.
   116	            //
   117	            // Note that this invariant might be
   118	            // true only because we modified
   119	            // `range` along the way.
   120	            //
   121	            // If `range` does not intertsect `existingRange`
   122	            // then our invariant will be trivially
   123	            // true for the next iteration.
   124	            //
   125	            if (!rangesOverlap(existingRange, range))
   126	            {
   127	                continue;
   128	            }
   129	
   130	            // We now know that `range` and `existingRange`
   131	            // intersect. The first thing to do
   132	            // is to check if we have a parameter
   133	            // associated with `existingRange`, so
   134	            // that we can use it for emitting diagnostics
   135	            // about the overlap:
   136	            //
   137	            if (existingRange.parameter && existingRange.parameter != newParam)
   138	            {
   139	                // There was an overlap with a range that
   140	                // had a parameter specified, so we will
   141	                // use that parameter in any subsequent
   142	                // diagnostics.
   143	                //
   144	                existingParam = existingRange.parameter;
   145	            }
   146	
   147	            // Before we can move on in our iteration,
   148	            // we need to re-establish our invariant by modifying
   149	            // `range` so that it doesn't overlap with `existingRange`.
   150	            // Of course we also want to end up with a correct
   151	            // result for the overall operation, so we can't just
   152	            // throw away intervals.
   153	            //
   154	            // We first note that if `range` starts before `existingRange`,
   155	            // then the interval from `range.begin` to `existingRange.begin`
   156	            // needs to be accounted for in the final result. Furthermore,
   157	            // the interval `[range.begin, existingRange.begin)` could not
   158	            // intersect with any range already in the `ranges` array,
   159	            // because it comes strictly before `existingRange`, and our
   160	            // invariant says there is no intersection with preceding ranges.
   161	            //
   162	            if (range.begin < existingRange.begin)
   163	            {
   164	                UsedRange prefix;
   165	                prefix.begin = range.begin;
   166	                prefix.end = existingRange.begin;
   167	                prefix.parameter = range.parameter;
   168	                ranges.add(prefix);
   169	            }
   170	            //
   171	            // Now we know that the interval `[range.begin, existingRange.begin)`
   172	            // is claimed, if it exists, and clearly the interval
   173	            // `[existingRange.begin, existingRange.end)` is already claimed,
   174	            // so the only interval left to consider would be
   175	            // `[existingRange.end, range.end)`, if it is non-empty.
   176	            // That range might intersect with others in the array, so
   177	            // we will need to continue iterating to deal with that
   178	            // possibility.
   179	            //
   180	            range.begin = existingRange.end;
   181	
   182	            // If the range would be empty, then of course we have nothing
   183	            // left to do.
   184	            //
   185	            if (range.begin >= range.end)
   186	                break;
   187	
   188	            // Otherwise, have can be sure that `range` now comes
   189	            // strictly *after* `existingRange`, and thus our invariant
   190	            // is preserved.
   191	        }
   192	
   193	        // If we manage to exit the loop, then we have resolved
   194	        // an intersection with existing entries - possibly by
   195	        // adding some new entries.
   196	        //
   197	        // If the `range` we are left with is still non-empty,
   198	        // then we should go ahead and add it.
   199	        //
   200	        if (range.begin < range.end)
   201	        {
   202	            ranges.add(range);
   203	        }
   204	
   205	        // Any ranges that got added along the way might not
   206	        // be in the proper sorted order, so we'll need to
   207	        // sort the array to restore our global invariant.
   208	        //
   209	        ranges.sort();
   210	
   211	        // We end by returning an overlapping parameter that
   212	        // we found along the way, if any.
   213	        //
   214	        return existingParam;
   215	    }
   216	
   217	    VarLayout* Add(VarLayout* param, UInt begin, UInt end)
   218	    {
   219	        UsedRange range;
   220	        range.parameter = param;
   221	        range.begin = begin;
   222	        range.end = end;
   223	        return Add(range);
   224	    }
   225	
   226	    VarLayout* Add(VarLayout* param, UInt begin, LayoutSize end)
   227	    {
   228	        UsedRange range;
   229	        range.parameter = param;
   230	        range.begin = begin;
   231	        range.end = end.isFinite() ? end.getFiniteValue() : UInt(-1);
   232	        return Add(range);
   233	    }
   234	
   235	    /// Finds the range that contains the index
   236	    /// Returns -1 if not found
   237	    Index findRangeContaining(UInt index) const
   238	    {
   239	        const auto rangeCount = ranges.getCount();
   240	        for (Index i = 0; i < rangeCount; ++i)
   241	        {
   242	            const auto& rr = ranges[i];
   243	            if (index >= rr.begin && index < rr.end)
   244	            {
   245	                return index;
   246	            }
   247	        }
   248	        return -1;
   249	    }
   250	    /// Finds the range index that contains the range passed in.
   251	    /// Returns -1 if not found
   252	    Index findRangeContaining(UInt index, UInt count) const
   253	    {
   254	        const auto start = index;
   255	        const auto end = index + count;
   256	
   257	        const auto rangeCount = ranges.getCount();
   258	        for (Index i = 0; i < rangeCount; ++i)
   259	        {
   260	            const auto& rr = ranges[i];
   261	
   262	            if (!(end <= rr.begin || start >= rr.end))
   263	            {
   264	                return i;
   265	            }
   266	        }
   267	        return -1;
   268	    }
   269	
   270	    Index findRangeContaining(UInt index, LayoutSize size) const
   271	    {
   272	        if (size.isFinite())
   273	        {
   274	            const auto count = size.getFiniteValue();
   275	            if (count > 0)
   276	            {
   277	                return (count == 1) ? findRangeContaining(index)
   278	                                    : findRangeContaining(index, count);
   279	            }
   280	        }
   281	        else
   282	        {
   283	            // The size is infinite...
   284	            const auto rangeCount = ranges.getCount();
   285	            for (Index i = 0; i < rangeCount; ++i)
   286	            {
   287	                // If the range end is part start index it's a hit
   288	                if (ranges[i].end > index)
   289	                {
   290	                    return i;
   291	                }
   292	            }
   293	        }
   294	        return -1;
   295	    }
   296	
   297	    bool contains(UInt index) const { return findRangeContaining(index) >= 0; }
   298	
   299	    // Try to find space for `count` entries
   300	    UInt Allocate(VarLayout* param, UInt count)
   301	    {
   302	        UInt begin = 0;
   303	
   304	        UInt rangeCount = ranges.getCount();
   305	        for (UInt rr = 0; rr < rangeCount; ++rr)
   306	        {
   307	            // try to fit in before this range...
   308	
   309	            UInt end = ranges[rr].begin;
   310	
   311	            // If there is enough space...
   312	            if (end >= begin + count)
   313	            {
   314	                // ... then claim it and be done
   315	                Add(param, begin, begin + count);
   316	                return begin;
   317	            }
   318	
   319	            // ... otherwise, we need to look at the
   320	            // space between this range and the next
   321	            begin = ranges[rr].end;
   322	        }
   323	
   324	        // We've run out of ranges to check, so we
   325	        // can safely go after the last one!
   326	        Add(param, begin, begin + count);
   327	        return begin;
   328	    }
   329	};

   476	static bool isDigit(char c)
   477	{
   478	    return (c >= '0') && (c <= '9');
   479	}
   480	
   481	bool splitNameAndIndex(
   482	    UnownedStringSlice const& text,
   483	    UnownedStringSlice& outName,
   484	    UnownedStringSlice& outDigits)
   485	{
   486	    char const* nameBegin = text.begin();
   487	    char const* digitsEnd = text.end();
   488	
   489	    char const* nameEnd = digitsEnd;
   490	    // ExplicitIndex is when a semantic has an index at the end of its name
   491	    // "SV_TARGET1" has an ExplicitIndex
   492	    // "SV_TARGET" does not have an ExplicitIndex
   493	    bool hasExplicitIndex = false;
   494	    while (nameEnd != nameBegin && isDigit(*(nameEnd - 1)))
   495	    {
   496	        hasExplicitIndex = true;
   497	        nameEnd--;
   498	    }
   499	    char const* digitsBegin = nameEnd;
   500	
   501	    outName = UnownedStringSlice(nameBegin, nameEnd);
   502	    outDigits = UnownedStringSlice(digitsBegin, digitsEnd);
   503	    return hasExplicitIndex;
   504	}
   505	
   506	LayoutResourceKind findRegisterClassFromName(UnownedStringSlice const& registerClassName)
   507	{
   508	    switch (registerClassName.getLength())
   509	    {
   510	    case 1:

  1284	        // We'll use inference from the HLSL like layout that will happen elsewhere
  1285	        return;
  1286	    }
  1287	
  1288	    const auto hlslInfo = _extractLayoutSemanticInfo(context, hlslRegSemantic);
  1289	    if (hlslInfo.kind == LayoutResourceKind::None)
  1290	    {
  1291	        // Doesn't have an HLSL resource consumption, so we are done
  1292	        return;
  1293	    }
  1294	
  1295	    // We can't infer TextureSampler from HLSL (it's not an HLSL concept)
  1296	    // So use default layout
  1297	    auto varType = getType(context->getASTBuilder(), varDecl.as<VarDeclBase>());
  1298	    if (auto textureType = as<TextureType>(varType))
  1299	    {
  1300	        if (textureType->isCombined())
  1301	        {
  1302	            if (!warnedMissingVulkanLayoutModifier)
  1303	            {
  1304	                _maybeDiagnoseMissingVulkanLayoutModifier(context, varDecl.as<VarDeclBase>());
  1305	                warnedMissingVulkanLayoutModifier = true;
  1306	            }
  1307	            return;
  1308	        }
  1309	    }
  1310	
  1311	    // Can we map to a Vulkan kind in principal?
  1312	    const HLSLToVulkanLayoutOptions::Kind vulkanKind =
  1313	        HLSLToVulkanLayoutOptions::getKind(hlslInfo.kind);
  1314	    if (vulkanKind == HLSLToVulkanLayoutOptions::Kind::Invalid)
  1315	    {
  1316	        // If we can't use inference, for the kind we'll use other mechanisms so we are done
  1317	        return;
  1318	    }
  1319	
  1320	    // If inference is not enabled for this kind, we can issue a warning
  1321	    if (hlslToVulkanLayoutOptions &&
  1322	        !hlslToVulkanLayoutOptions->canInfer(vulkanKind, hlslInfo.space))
  1323	    {
  1324	        if (!warnedMissingVulkanLayoutModifier)
  1325	        {
  1326	            _maybeDiagnoseMissingVulkanLayoutModifier(context, varDecl.as<VarDeclBase>());
  1327	            warnedMissingVulkanLayoutModifier = true;
  1328	        }
  1329	    }
  1330	
  1331	    if (warnedMissingVulkanLayoutModifier)
  1332	    {
  1333	        // If we warn due to invalid bindings and user did not set how to interpret 'hlsl style
  1334	        // bindings', we should map `register` 1:1 with equivlent vulkan bindings.
  1335	        if (!hlslToVulkanLayoutOptions || hlslToVulkanLayoutOptions->getKindShiftEnabledFlags() ==
  1336	                                              HLSLToVulkanLayoutOptions::KindFlag::None)
  1337	        {
  1338	            info[kResInfo].resInfo =
  1339	                typeLayout->findOrAddResourceInfo(LayoutResourceKind::DescriptorTableSlot);
  1340	            info[kResInfo].resInfo->count = 1;
  1341	        }
  1342	        else
  1343	        {
  1344	            return;
  1345	        }
  1346	    }
  1347	
  1348	    // We use the HLSL binding directly (even though this notionally for GLSL/Vulkan)
  1349	    // We'll do the shifting at later later point in _maybeApplyHLSLToVulkanShifts
  1350	    if (!info[kResInfo].resInfo)

     1	// slang-hlsl-to-vulkan-layout-options.h
     2	#ifndef SLANG_HLSL_TO_VULKAN_LAYOUT_OPTIONS_H
     3	#define SLANG_HLSL_TO_VULKAN_LAYOUT_OPTIONS_H
     4	
     5	#include "../core/slang-basic.h"
     6	#include "../core/slang-name-value.h"
     7	
     8	namespace Slang
     9	{
    10	
    11	/*
    12	For support features similar to described here..
    13	
    14	https://github.com/microsoft/DirectXShaderCompiler/blob/main/docs/SPIR-V.rst#descriptors
    15	
    16	Options that allow for infering Vulkan bindings based on HLSL register bindings
    17	  */
    18	
    19	struct CompilerOptionSet;
    20	
    21	struct HLSLToVulkanLayoutOptions : public RefObject
    22	{
    23	public:
    24	    static const Index kInvalidShift = Index(0x80000000);
    25	
    26	    /// For holding combination of set and index for binding
    27	    struct Binding
    28	    {
    29	        bool isSet() const { return set >= 0 && index >= 0; }
    30	        void reset()
    31	        {
    32	            set = -1;
    33	            index = -1;
    34	        }
    35	        bool isInvalid() const { return !isSet(); }
    36	
    37	        Index set = -1;
    38	        Index index = -1;
    39	    };
    40	
    41	    // https://github.com/KhronosGroup/glslang/wiki/HLSL-FAQ
    42	    // {b|s|t|u}
    43	    enum class Kind
    44	    {
    45	        Invalid = -1,
    46	
    47	        /// Unordered access view (u)
    48	        ///
    49	        /// RWByteAddressBuffer/RWStructuredBuffer
    50	        /// Append/ConsumeStructuredBuffer
    51	        /// RWBuffer
    52	        /// RWTextureXD/Array
    53	        UnorderedAccess = 0,
    54	
    55	        /// Sampler (s)
    56	        ///
    57	        /// SamplerXD
    58	        /// SamplerState/SamplerComparisonState
    59	        Sampler,
    60	
    61	        /// Shader Resource (t)
    62	        ///
    63	        /// TextureXD/Array
    64	        /// ByteAddressBuffer/StructuredBuffer/Buffer/TBuffer
    65	        ShaderResource,
    66	
    67	        /// Constant buffer (b)
    68	        ///
    69	        /// ConstantBufferViews, CBuffer
    70	        ConstantBuffer,
    71	
    72	        CountOf,
    73	    };
    74	
    75	    // A flag for each kind
    76	    typedef uint32_t KindFlags;
    77	    struct KindFlag
    78	    {
    79	        enum Enum : KindFlags
    80	        {
    81	            None = 0,
    82	            UnorderedAccess = KindFlags(1) << Index(Kind::UnorderedAccess),
    83	            Sampler = KindFlags(1) << Index(Kind::Sampler),
    84	            ShaderResource = KindFlags(1) << Index(Kind::ShaderResource),
    85	            ConstantBuffer = KindFlags(1) << Index(Kind::ConstantBuffer),
    86	        };
    87	    };
    88	
    89	    /// Get a kind flag from a kind
    90	    SLANG_FORCE_INLINE static KindFlag::Enum getKindFlag(Kind kind)
    91	    {
    92	        SLANG_ASSERT(kind != Kind::Invalid);
    93	        return KindFlag::Enum(KindFlags(1) << Index(kind));
    94	    }
    95	
    96	    struct Key
    97	    {
    98	        typedef Key ThisType;
    99	
   100	        bool operator==(const ThisType& rhs) const { return kind == rhs.kind && set == rhs.set; }
   101	        bool operator!=(const ThisType& rhs) const { return !(*this == rhs); }
   102	
   103	        HashCode getHashCode() const
   104	        {
   105	            return combineHash(Slang::getHashCode(kind), Slang::getHashCode(set));
   106	        }
   107	
   108	        Kind kind; ///< The kind this entry is for
   109	        Index set; ///< The set this shift is associated with
   110	    };
   111	
   112	    /// Set the the all option for the kind.
   113	    void setAllShift(Kind kind, Index shift);
   114	
   115	    /// Set the shift for kind/set
   116	    void setShift(Kind kind, Index set, Index shift);
   117	
   118	    /// Get the shift. Returns kInvalidShift if no shift is found
   119	    Index getShift(Kind kind, Index set) const;
   120	
   121	    /// True as global binds set
   122	    bool hasGlobalsBinding() const { return m_globalsBinding.isSet(); }
   123	
   124	    /// True if holds state such that vulkan bindings can be inferred from HLSL bindings
   125	    bool canInferBindings() const { return m_kindShiftEnabledFlags != 0; }
   126	
   127	    /// True if the kind/set can be inferred
   128	    bool canInfer(Kind kind, Index set) const { return getShift(kind, set) != kInvalidShift; }
   129	
   130	    /// True if can infer a binding for a kind
   131	    bool canInferBindingForKind(Kind kind) const
   132	    {
   133	        return (m_kindShiftEnabledFlags & getKindFlag(kind)) != 0;
   134	    }
   135	
   136	    bool shouldUseGLLayout() const { return m_useGLLayout; }
   137	
   138	    bool shouldEmitSPIRVReflectionInfo() const { return m_emitSPIRVReflectionInfo; }
   139	
   140	    bool getUseOriginalEntryPointName() const { return m_useOriginalEntryPointName; }
   141	
   142	    /// Given an kind and a binding infer the vulkan binding.
   143	    /// Will return an invalid binding if one is not found
   144	    Binding inferBinding(Kind kind, const Binding& inBinding) const;
   145	
   146	    /// Returns flags indicating for each kind if there is shift inference
   147	    KindFlags getKindShiftEnabledFlags() const { return m_kindShiftEnabledFlags; }
   148	
   149	    /// Reset state such that all options are set to their default. The same state as when
   150	    /// originally constructed
   151	    void reset();
   152	
   153	    /// Returns true if any state is set
   154	    bool hasState() const;
   155	
   156	    /// Returns true if contains default reset state. If so it can in effect be ignored
   157	    bool isReset() const { return !hasState(); }
   158	
   159	    /// Set the global binding
   160	    void setGlobalsBinding(Index set, Index bindingIndex)
   161	    {
   162	        setGlobalsBinding(Binding{set, bindingIndex});
   163	    }
   164	    /// Set the global bindings
   165	    void setGlobalsBinding(const Binding& binding);
   166	    /// Get the globals binding
   167	    const Binding& getGlobalsBinding() const { return m_globalsBinding; }
   168	
   169	    void setUseOriginalEntryPointName(bool value) { m_useOriginalEntryPointName = value; }
   170	
   171	    void setUseGLLayout(bool value) { m_useGLLayout = value; }
   172	
   173	    void setEmitSPIRVReflectionInfo(bool value) { m_emitSPIRVReflectionInfo = value; }
   174	
   175	    void loadFromOptionSet(CompilerOptionSet& optionSet);
   176	
   177	    /// Ctor
   178	    HLSLToVulkanLayoutOptions();
   179	
   180	    /// Get information about the different kinds
   181	    static ConstArrayView<NamesDescriptionValue> getKindInfos();
   182	
   183	    /// Given a paramCategory get the kind. Returns Kind::Invalid if not an applicable category
   184	    static Kind getKind(slang::ParameterCategory param);
   185	
   186	protected:
   187	    /// Marks that a shift is enabled for the kind
   188	    void _enableShiftForKind(Kind kind) { m_kindShiftEnabledFlags |= getKindFlag(kind); }
   189	
   190	    Binding m_globalsBinding;
   191	
   192	    /// The `all` shifts
   193	    Index m_allShifts[Count(Kind::CountOf)];
   194	
   195	    /// Holds a bit for each kind that has a shift enabled
   196	    KindFlags m_kindShiftEnabledFlags = 0;
   197	
   198	    /// Maps a key to the amount of shift
   199	    Dictionary<Key, Index> m_shifts;
   200	
   201	    /// If set, will use the original entry point name in the generated SPIRV instead of "main".
   202	    bool m_useOriginalEntryPointName = false;
   203	
   204	    /// If set, raw buffer load/stores will follow std430 layout.
   205	    bool m_useGLLayout = false;
   206	
   207	    /// If set, will emit SPIR-V reflection info.
   208	    bool m_emitSPIRVReflectionInfo = false;
   209	};

  1072	static void _maybeDiagnoseMissingVulkanLayoutModifier(
  1073	    ParameterBindingContext* context,
  1074	    DeclRef<VarDeclBase> const& varDecl)
  1075	{
  1076	    // Don't warn if the declaration is a vk::push_constant or shaderRecordEXT
  1077	    if (varDecl.getDecl()->hasModifier<PushConstantAttribute>() ||
  1078	        varDecl.getDecl()->hasModifier<ShaderRecordAttribute>())
  1079	    {
  1080	        return;
  1081	    }
  1082	
  1083	    // If the user didn't specify a `binding` (and optional `set`) for Vulkan,
  1084	    // but they *did* specify a `register` for D3D, then that is probably an
  1085	    // oversight on their part.
  1086	    if (auto registerModifier = varDecl.getDecl()->findModifier<HLSLRegisterSemantic>())
  1087	    {
  1088	        auto varType = getType(context->getASTBuilder(), varDecl.as<VarDeclBase>());
  1089	        if (auto textureType = as<TextureType>(varType))
  1090	        {
  1091	            if (textureType->isCombined())
  1092	            {
  1093	                // Recommend [[vk::binding]] but not '-fvk-xxx-shift` for combined texture samplers
  1094	                getSink(context)->diagnose(
  1095	                    registerModifier,
  1096	                    Diagnostics::registerModifierButNoVulkanLayout,
  1097	                    varDecl.getName());
  1098	                return;
  1099	            }
  1100	        }
  1101	
  1102	        UnownedStringSlice registerClassName;
  1103	        UnownedStringSlice registerIndexDigits;
  1104	        splitNameAndIndex(
  1105	            registerModifier->registerName.getContent(),
  1106	            registerClassName,
  1107	            registerIndexDigits);
  1108	
  1109	        getSink(context)->diagnose(
  1110	            registerModifier,
  1111	            Diagnostics::registerModifierButNoVkBindingNorShift,
  1112	            varDecl.getName(),
  1113	            registerClassName);
  1114	    }
  1115	}

    10	#include <assert.h>
    11	
    12	namespace Slang
    13	{
    14	
    15	static bool _isPow2(size_t v)
    16	{
    17	    return v > 0 && ((v - 1) & v) == 0;
    18	}
    19	
    20	static size_t _roundToAlignment(size_t offset, size_t alignment)
    21	{
    22	    // Must also be a power of 2
    23	    SLANG_ASSERT(_isPow2(alignment));
    24	
    25	    const size_t mask = alignment - 1;
    26	    return (offset + mask) & ~mask;
    27	}
    28	
    29	static LayoutSize _roundToAlignment(LayoutSize offset, size_t alignment)
    30	{
    31	    // An infinite size is assumed to be maximally aligned.
    32	    if (offset.isInfinite())
    33	        return LayoutSize::infinite();
    34	
    35	    return _roundToAlignment(offset.getFiniteValue(), alignment);
    36	}
    37	
    38	static size_t _roundUpToPowerOfTwo(size_t value)
    39	{
    40	    // TODO(tfoley): I know this isn't a fast approach
    41	    size_t result = 1;
    42	    while (result < value)
    43	        result *= 2;
    44	    return result;
    45	}
    46	
    47	static bool _isAligned(size_t size, size_t alignment)
    48	{
    49	    SLANG_ASSERT(_isPow2(alignment));
    50	    return ((alignment - 1) & size) == 0;
    51	}

    60	    SLANG_UNUSED(b);

   974	static void addExplicitParameterBindings_HLSL(
   975	    ParameterBindingContext* context,
   976	    RefPtr<ParameterInfo> parameterInfo,
   977	    RefPtr<VarLayout> varLayout)
   978	{
   979	    // We only want to apply D3D `register` modifiers when compiling for
   980	    // D3D and Metal targets.
   981	    //
   982	    // TODO: Nominally, the `register` keyword allows for a shader
   983	    // profile to be specified, so that a given binding only
   984	    // applies for a specific profile:
   985	    //
   986	    //      https://docs.microsoft.com/en-us/windows/desktop/direct3dhlsl/dx-graphics-hlsl-variable-register
   987	    //
   988	    // We might want to consider supporting that syntax in the
   989	    // long run, in order to handle bindings for multiple targets
   990	    // in a more consistent fashion (whereas using `register` for D3D
   991	    // and `[[vk::binding(...)]]` for Vulkan creates a lot of
   992	    // visual noise).
   993	    //
   994	    // For now we do the filtering on target in a very direct fashion:
   995	    //
   996	    bool isMetal = isMetalTarget(context->getTargetRequest());
   997	    if (!isD3DTarget(context->getTargetRequest()) && !isMetal)
   998	        return;
   999	
  1000	    auto typeLayout = varLayout->typeLayout;
  1001	    auto varDecl = varLayout->varDecl;
  1002	
  1003	    // If the declaration has explicit binding modifiers, then
  1004	    // here is where we want to extract and apply them...
  1005	    if (auto inputAttachmentIndexLayoutAttribute =
  1006	            varDecl.getDecl()->findModifier<GLSLInputAttachmentIndexLayoutAttribute>())
  1007	    {
  1008	        LayoutSemanticInfo semanticInfo;
  1009	        semanticInfo.index = (UInt)inputAttachmentIndexLayoutAttribute->location;
  1010	        semanticInfo.space = 0;
  1011	        semanticInfo.kind = LayoutResourceKind::InputAttachmentIndex;
  1012	
  1013	        if (auto varDeclBase = varDecl.as<VarDeclBase>())
  1014	            addExplicitParameterBinding(
  1015	                context,
  1016	                parameterInfo,
  1017	                varDeclBase.getDecl(),
  1018	                semanticInfo,
  1019	                1);
  1020	    }
  1021	
  1022	    // Look for HLSL `register` or `packoffset` semantics.
  1023	    for (auto semantic : varDecl.getDecl()->getModifiersOfType<HLSLLayoutSemantic>())
  1024	    {
  1025	        // Need to extract the information encoded in the semantic
  1026	        LayoutSemanticInfo semanticInfo = _extractLayoutSemanticInfo(context, semantic);
  1027	        auto kind = semanticInfo.kind;
  1028	        if (kind == LayoutResourceKind::None)
  1029	            continue;
  1030

   626	    ParameterBindingContext* context,
   627	    HLSLLayoutSemantic* semantic)
   628	{
   629	    Token const& registerToken = semantic->registerName;
   630	
   631	    Token defaultSpaceToken;
   632	    Token const* spaceToken = &defaultSpaceToken;
   633	    if (auto registerSemantic = as<HLSLRegisterSemantic>(semantic))

   541	    UnownedStringSlice registerName,
   542	    SourceLoc registerLoc,

   544	    SourceLoc spaceLoc,
   545	    DiagnosticSink* sink)
   546	{
   547	    LayoutSemanticInfo info;
   548	    info.space = 0;
   549	    info.index = 0;
   550	    info.kind = LayoutResourceKind::None;
   551	
   552	    if (registerName.getLength() == 0)
   553	        return info;
   554	
   555	    // The register name is expected to be in the form:
   556	    //
   557	    //      identifier-char+ digit+
   558	    //
   559	    // where the identifier characters name a "register class"
   560	    // and the digits identify a register index within that class.
   561	    //
   562	    // We are going to split the string the user gave us
   563	    // into these constituent parts:
   564	    //
   565	    UnownedStringSlice registerClassName;
   566	    UnownedStringSlice registerIndexDigits;
   567	    splitNameAndIndex(registerName, registerClassName, registerIndexDigits);
   568	
   569	    LayoutResourceKind kind = findRegisterClassFromName(registerClassName);
   570	    if (kind == LayoutResourceKind::None)
   571	    {
   572	        sink->diagnose(registerLoc, Diagnostics::unknownRegisterClass, registerClassName);
   573	        return info;
   574	    }
   575	
   576	    // For a `register` semantic, the register index is not optional (unlike
   577	    // how it works for varying input/output semantics).
   578	    if (registerIndexDigits.getLength() == 0)
   579	    {
   580	        sink->diagnose(registerLoc, Diagnostics::expectedARegisterIndex, registerClassName);

  1377	// Given a single parameter, collect whatever information we have on
  1378	// how it has been explicitly bound, which may come from multiple declarations
  1379	void _generateParameterBindings(
  1380	    ParameterBindingContext* context,
  1381	    RefPtr<ParameterInfo> parameterInfo)
  1382	{
  1383	    // There must have been a declaration for the parameter.
  1384	    SLANG_RELEASE_ASSERT(parameterInfo->varLayout);
  1385	
  1386	    // We will look for explicit binding information on the declaration.
  1387	    auto varLayout = parameterInfo->varLayout;
  1388	
  1389	    // Handle HLSL `register` and `packoffset` modifiers
  1390	    addExplicitParameterBindings_HLSL(context, parameterInfo, varLayout);
  1391	
  1392	
  1393	    // Handle GLSL `layout` modifiers and `[vk::...]` attributes.
  1394	    //
  1395	    // TODO: We should deprecate the support for `layout` and then rename
  1396	    // these `_HLSL` and `_GLSL` functions to be more explicit and clear
  1397	    // about the fact that they are specific to the *target* and not to
  1398	    // the *source language* (as they were at one point).
  1399	    //
  1400	    addExplicitParameterBindings_GLSL(context, parameterInfo, varLayout);
  1401	}
